5035      * other than {@code S1 -> T1, S2 -> T2, ... Sn -> Tn} where {@code T1, T2 ... Tn} are the coordinate types starting
5036      * at position {@code pos} of the target var handle, if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target var handle coordinate arity, inclusive,
5037      * or if more filters are provided than the actual number of coordinate types, or if any of the filters throws any
5038      * checked exceptions.
5039      * available starting at {@code pos}.
5040      */
5041     public static VarHandle filterCoordinates(VarHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5042         Objects.nonNull(target);
5043         Objects.nonNull(filters);
5044         if (filters.length == 0) return target;
5045 
5046         List<Class<?>> targetCoordinates = target.coordinateTypes();
5047         if (pos < 0 || pos >= targetCoordinates.size()) {
5048             throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid position " + pos + " for coordinate types", targetCoordinates);
5049         } else if (pos + filters.length > targetCoordinates.size()) {
5050             throw new IllegalArgumentException("Too many filters");
5051         }
5052 
5053         List<Class<?>> newCoordinates = new ArrayList<>(targetCoordinates);
5054         for (int i = 0 ; i < filters.length ; i++) {
5055             noCheckedExceptions(filters[i]);
5056             MethodType filterType = filters[i].type();
5057             if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1) {
5058                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid filter type " + filterType);
5059             } else if (newCoordinates.get(pos + i) != filterType.returnType()) {
5060                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid filter type " + filterType + " for coordinate type " + newCoordinates.get(i));
5061             }
5062             newCoordinates.set(pos + i, filters[i].type().parameterType(0));
5063         }
5064 
5065         return new IndirectVarHandle(target, target.varType(), newCoordinates.toArray(new Class<?>[0]),
5066                 (mode, modeHandle) -> MethodHandles.filterArguments(modeHandle, 1 + pos, filters));
5067     }
5068 
5069     /**
5070      * Provides a target var handle with one or more <em>bound coordinates</em>
5071      * in advance of the var handle's invocation. As a consequence, the resulting var handle will feature less
5072      * coordinate types than the target var handle.
5073      * <p>
5074      * When calling e.g. {@link VarHandle#get(Object...)} on the resulting var handle, incoming coordinate values
5075      * are joined with bound coordinate values, and then passed to the target var handle.
5076      * <p>
5077      * For the bound coordinates to be well formed, their types must be {@code T1, T2 ... Tn },
5078      * where {@code T1, T2 ... Tn} are the coordinate types starting at position {@code pos} of the target var handle.
5079      * <p>
5080      * The resulting var handle will feature the same access modes (see {@link java.lang.invoke.VarHandle.AccessMode} and
5081      * atomic access guarantees as those featured by the target var handle.
5082      *
5083      * @param target the var handle to invoke after the bound coordinates are inserted
5084      * @param pos the position of the first coordinate to be inserted
5085      * @param values the series of bound coordinates to insert
5086      * @return an adapter var handle which inserts an additional coordinates,
5087      *         before calling the target var handle
5088      * @throws NullPointerException if either {@code target}, {@code values} are {@code == null}.
5089      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target var handle coordinate arity, inclusive,
5090      * or if more values are provided than the actual number of coordinate types available starting at {@code pos}.
5091      * @throws ClassCastException if the bound coordinates in {@code values} are not well-formed, that is, they have types
5092      * other than {@code T1, T2 ... Tn }, where {@code T1, T2 ... Tn} are the coordinate types starting at position {@code pos}
5093      * of the target var handle.
5094      */
5095     public static VarHandle insertCoordinates(VarHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
5096         Objects.nonNull(target);
5097         Objects.nonNull(values);
5098         if (values.length == 0) return target;
5099 
5100         List<Class<?>> targetCoordinates = target.coordinateTypes();
5101         if (pos < 0 || pos >= targetCoordinates.size()) {
5102             throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid position " + pos + " for coordinate types", targetCoordinates);
5103         } else if (pos + values.length > targetCoordinates.size()) {
5104             throw new IllegalArgumentException("Too many values");
5105         }
5106 
5107         List<Class<?>> newCoordinates = new ArrayList<>(targetCoordinates);
5108         for (int i = 0 ; i < values.length ; i++) {
5109             Class<?> pt = newCoordinates.get(pos);
5110             if (pt.isPrimitive()) {
5111                 Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(pt);
5112                 w.convert(values[i], pt);
5113             } else {
5114                 pt.cast(values[i]);
5115             }
5116             newCoordinates.remove(pos);
5117         }
5118 
5119         return new IndirectVarHandle(target, target.varType(), newCoordinates.toArray(new Class<?>[0]),
5120                 (mode, modeHandle) -> MethodHandles.insertArguments(modeHandle, 1 + pos, values));
5121     }
5122 
5123     /**
5124      * Provides a var handle which adapts the coordinate values of the target var handle, by re-arranging them
5125      * so that the new coordinates match the provided ones.
5126      * <p>
5127      * The given array controls the reordering.
5128      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming coordinates (the value
5129      * {@code newCoordinates.size()}, and call {@code #O} the number
5130      * of outgoing coordinates (the number of coordinates associated with the target var handle).
5131      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
5132      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
5133      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
5134      * outgoing coordinate will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
5135      * coordinate, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
5136      * <p>
5137      * No coordinate value conversions are applied.
5138      * The type of each incoming coordinate, as determined by {@code newCoordinates},
5139      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing coordinate
5140      * in the target var handle.
5141      * <p>
5142      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
5143      * An incoming coordinate will be duplicated if its index appears
5144      * more than once in the array, and an incoming coordinate will be dropped
5145      * if its index does not appear in the array.
5146      * <p>
5147      * The resulting var handle will feature the same access modes (see {@link java.lang.invoke.VarHandle.AccessMode} and
5148      * atomic access guarantees as those featured by the target var handle.
5149      * @param target the var handle to invoke after the coordinates have been reordered
5150      * @param newCoordinates the new coordinate types
5151      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
5152      * @return an adapter var handle which re-arranges the incoming coordinate values,
5153      * before calling the target var handle
5154      * @throws NullPointerException if either {@code target}, {@code newCoordinates} or {@code reorder} are {@code == null}.
5155      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
5156      * the number of coordinates of the target var handle, or if any index array element is not a valid index for
5157      * a coordinate of {@code newCoordinates}, or if two corresponding coordinate types in
5158      * the target var handle and in {@code newCoordinates} are not identical.
5159      */
5160     public static VarHandle permuteCoordinates(VarHandle target, List<Class<?>> newCoordinates, int... reorder) {
5161         Objects.nonNull(target);
5162         Objects.nonNull(newCoordinates);
5163         Objects.nonNull(reorder);
5164 
5165         List<Class<?>> targetCoordinates = target.coordinateTypes();
5166         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder,
5167                 MethodType.methodType(void.class, newCoordinates),
5168                 MethodType.methodType(void.class, targetCoordinates));
5169 
5170         return new IndirectVarHandle(target, target.varType(), newCoordinates.toArray(new Class<?>[0]),
5171                 (mode, modeHandle) ->
5172                     MethodHandles.permuteArguments(modeHandle,
5173                         methodTypeFor(mode.at, modeHandle.type(), targetCoordinates, newCoordinates),
5174                         reorderArrayFor(mode.at, newCoordinates, reorder)));
5175     }
5176 
5177     private static int numTrailingArgs(VarHandle.AccessType at) {
5178         return switch (at) {
5179             case GET -> 0;
5180             case GET_AND_UPDATE, SET -> 1;
5181             case COMPARE_AND_SET, COMPARE_AND_EXCHANGE -> 2;
5182         };
5183     }
5184 
5185     private static int[] reorderArrayFor(VarHandle.AccessType at, List<Class<?>> newCoordinates, int[] reorder) {
5186         int numTrailingArgs = numTrailingArgs(at);
5187         int[] adjustedReorder = new int[reorder.length + 1 + numTrailingArgs];
5188         adjustedReorder[0] = 0;
5189         for (int i = 0 ; i < reorder.length ; i++) {
5190             adjustedReorder[i + 1] = reorder[i] + 1;
5191         }
5192         for (int i = 0 ; i < numTrailingArgs ; i++) {
5193             adjustedReorder[i + reorder.length + 1] = i + newCoordinates.size() + 1;
5194         }
5195         return adjustedReorder;
5196     }
5197 
5198     private static MethodType methodTypeFor(VarHandle.AccessType at, MethodType oldType, List<Class<?>> oldCoordinates, List<Class<?>> newCoordinates) {
5199         int numTrailingArgs = numTrailingArgs(at);
5200         MethodType adjustedType = MethodType.methodType(oldType.returnType(), oldType.parameterType(0));
5201         adjustedType = adjustedType.appendParameterTypes(newCoordinates);
5202         for (int i = 0 ; i < numTrailingArgs ; i++) {
5203             adjustedType = adjustedType.appendParameterTypes(oldType.parameterType(1 + oldCoordinates.size() + i));
5204         }
5205         return adjustedType;
5206     }
5207 
5208     /**
5209      * Adapts a target var handle handle by pre-processing
5210      * a sub-sequence of its coordinate values with a filter (a method handle).
5211      * The pre-processed coordinates are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5212      * filter function and the target var handle is then called on the modified (usually shortened)
5213      * coordinate list.
5214      * <p>
5215      * If {code R} is the return type of the filter (which cannot be void), the target var handle must accept a value of
5216      * type {@code R} as its coordinate in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5217      * any coordinate not passed to the filter.
5218      * No coordinates are reordered, and the result returned from the filter
5219      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of coordinates originally
5220      * passed to the adapter.
5221      * <p>
5222      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5223      * replace zero or one coordinate types of the target var handle, at position {@code pos},
5224      * in the resulting adapted var handle.
5225      * The return type of the filter must be identical to the
5226      * coordinate type of the target var handle at position {@code pos}, and that target var handle
5227      * coordinate is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5228      * <p>
5229      * The resulting var handle will feature the same access modes (see {@link java.lang.invoke.VarHandle.AccessMode} and
5230      * atomic access guarantees as those featured by the target var handle.
5231      *
5232      * @param target the var handle to invoke after the coordinates have been filtered
5233      * @param pos the position of the coordinate to be filtered
5234      * @param filter the filter method handle
5235      * @return an adapter var handle which filters the incoming coordinate values,
5236      * before calling the target var handle
5237      * @throws NullPointerException if either {@code target}, {@code filter} are {@code == null}.
5238      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5239      * is void, or it is not the same as the {@code pos} coordinate of the target var handle,
5240      * if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target var handle coordinate arity, inclusive,
5241      * if the resulting var handle's type would have <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many coordinates</a>,
5242      * or if {@code filter} throws any checked exceptions.
5243      */
5244     public static VarHandle collectCoordinates(VarHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5245         Objects.nonNull(target);
5246         Objects.nonNull(filter);
5247         noCheckedExceptions(filter);
5248 
5249         List<Class<?>> targetCoordinates = target.coordinateTypes();
5250         if (pos < 0 || pos >= targetCoordinates.size()) {
5251             throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid position " + pos + " for coordinate types", targetCoordinates);
5252         } else if (filter.type().returnType() == void.class) {
5253             throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid filter type " + filter.type() + " ; filter cannot be void");
5254         } else if (filter.type().returnType() != targetCoordinates.get(pos)) {
5255             throw newIllegalArgumentException("Invalid filter type " + filter.type() + " for coordinate type " + targetCoordinates.get(pos));
5256         }
5257 
5258         List<Class<?>> newCoordinates = new ArrayList<>(targetCoordinates);
5259         for (Class<?> arg : filter.type().parameterList()) {
5260             newCoordinates.add(pos, arg);
5261         }
5262 
5263         return new IndirectVarHandle(target, target.varType(), newCoordinates.toArray(new Class<?>[0]),
5264                 (mode, modeHandle) -> MethodHandles.collectArguments(modeHandle, 1 + pos, filter));
5265     }
5266 
5267     private static void noCheckedExceptions(MethodHandle handle) {
5268         if (handle instanceof DirectMethodHandle) {
5269             DirectMethodHandle directHandle = (DirectMethodHandle)handle;
5270             MethodHandleInfo info = Lookup.IMPL_LOOKUP.revealDirect(directHandle);
5271             Class<?>[] exceptionTypes = switch (info.getReferenceKind()) {
5272                 case MethodHandleInfo.REF_invokeInterface, MethodHandleInfo.REF_invokeSpecial,
5273                      MethodHandleInfo.REF_invokeStatic, MethodHandleInfo.REF_invokeVirtual ->
5274                         info.reflectAs(Method.class, Lookup.IMPL_LOOKUP).getExceptionTypes();
5275                 case MethodHandleInfo.REF_newInvokeSpecial ->
5276                         info.reflectAs(Constructor.class, Lookup.IMPL_LOOKUP).getExceptionTypes();
5277                 case MethodHandleInfo.REF_getField, MethodHandleInfo.REF_getStatic,
5278                      MethodHandleInfo.REF_putField, MethodHandleInfo.REF_putStatic -> null;
5279                 default -> throw new AssertionError("Cannot get here");
5280             };
5281             if (exceptionTypes != null) {
5282                 if (Stream.of(exceptionTypes).anyMatch(MethodHandles::isCheckedException)) {
5283                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("Cannot adapt a var handle with a method handle which throws checked exceptions");
5284                 }
5285             }
5286         } else if (handle instanceof DelegatingMethodHandle) {
5287             noCheckedExceptions(((DelegatingMethodHandle)handle).getTarget());
5288         } else {
5289             //bound
5290             BoundMethodHandle boundHandle = (BoundMethodHandle)handle;
5291             for (int i = 0 ; i < boundHandle.fieldCount() ; i++) {
5292                 Object arg = boundHandle.arg(i);
5293                 if (arg instanceof MethodHandle){
5294                     noCheckedExceptions((MethodHandle) arg);
5295                 }
5296             }
5297         }
5298     }
5299 
5300     private static boolean isCheckedException(Class<?> clazz) {
5301         return Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(clazz) &&
5302                 !RuntimeException.class.isAssignableFrom(clazz) &&
5303                 !Error.class.isAssignableFrom(clazz);
5304     }
5305 
5306     /**
5307      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5308      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5309      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5310      * sequence of arguments.
5311      * <p>
5312      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5313      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5314      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5315      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5316      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5317      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5318      * arguments.
5319      * <p>
5320      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5321      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5322      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5323      * of the combiner.
5324      * <p>
5325      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5326      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5327      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5328      * <p>
5329      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5330      * first parameter type is dropped,
5331      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5332      * <p>
5333      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5334      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5335      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5336      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5337      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5338      * target.)
5339      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5340      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5341 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5342 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5343 ...
5344 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5345   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5346     .bindTo(System.out);
5347 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5348   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5349 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5350 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5351 // also prints "boo":
5352 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5353      * }</pre></blockquote>
5354      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5355      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5356      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5357      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5358      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5359      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5360      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5361      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5362      * and arguments.
5363      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5364      * // there are N arguments in A...
5365      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5366      * V combiner(A...);
5367      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5368      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5369      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5370      * }
5371      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5372      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5373      * void combiner2(A...);
5374      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5375      *   combiner2(a...);
5376      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5377      * }
5378      * }</pre></blockquote>
5379      * <p>
5380      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5381      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5382      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5383      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5384      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5385      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5386      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5387      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5388      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5389      *          of the target
5390      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5391      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5392      */
5393     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5394         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5395     }
5396 
5397     /**
5398      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5399      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5400      * before the folded arguments.
5401      * <p>
5402      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5403      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5404      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5405      * 0.
5406      *
5407      * @apiNote Example:
5408      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5409     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5410     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5411     ...
5412     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5413     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5414     .bindTo(System.out);
5415     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5416     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5417     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5418     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5419     // also prints "jum":
5420     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5421      * }</pre></blockquote>
5422      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5423      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5424      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5425      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5426      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5427      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5428      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5429      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5430      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5431      * respectively.
5432      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5433      * // there are N arguments in A...
5434      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5435      * V combiner(A...);
5436      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5437      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5438      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5439      * }
5440      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5441      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5442      * void combiner2(A...);
5443      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5444      *   combiner2(a...);
5445      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5446      * }
5447      * }</pre></blockquote>
5448      * <p>
5449      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5450      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5451      *
5452      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5453      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5454      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5455      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5456      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5457      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5458      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5459      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5460      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5461      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5462      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5463      *
5464      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5465      * @since 9
5466      */
5467     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5468         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5469         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5470         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5471         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5472         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5473         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5474         MethodType newType = targetType;
5475         if (!dropResult) {
5476             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5477         }
5478         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5479         return result;
5480     }
5481 
5482     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5483         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5484         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5485         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5486         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5487         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5488         if (ok) {
5489             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5490                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5491                     ok = false;
5492                     break;
5493                 }
5494             }
5495         }
5496         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5497             ok = false;
5498         if (!ok)
5499             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5500         return rtype;
5501     }
5502 
5503     /**
5504      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5505      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5506      *
5507      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5508      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5509      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5510      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5511      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5512      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5513      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5514      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5515      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5516      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5517      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5518      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5519      */
5520     /*non-public*/
5521     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5522         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5523     }
5524 
5525     /**
5526      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5527      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5528      *
5529      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5530      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5531      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5532      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5533      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5534      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5535      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5536      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5537      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5538      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5539      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5540      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5541      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5542      */
5543     /*non-public*/
5544     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5545         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5546     }
5547 
5548     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5549         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5550         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5551         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5552         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5553 
5554         MethodType newType = targetType;
5555         LambdaForm lform;
5556         if (filter) {
5557             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5558         } else {
5559             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5560             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5561             if (!dropResult) {
5562                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5563             }
5564         }
5565         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5566         return result;
5567     }
5568 
5569     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5570         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5571         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5572             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5573         }
5574         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5575 
5576         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5577             int arg = argPos[i];
5578             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5579                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5580             }
5581             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5582                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5583                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5584                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5585             }
5586         }
5587         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5588             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5589         }
5590         return rtype;
5591     }
5592 
5593     /**
5594      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5595      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5596      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5597      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5598      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5599      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5600      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5601      * <p>
5602      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5603      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5604      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5605      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5606      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5607      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5608      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5609      * boolean test(A...);
5610      * T target(A...,B...);
5611      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5612      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5613      *   if (test(a...))
5614      *     return target(a..., b...);
5615      *   else
5616      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5617      * }
5618      * }</pre></blockquote>
5619      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5620      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5621      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5622      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5623      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5624      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5625      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5626      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5627      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5628      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5629      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5630      */
5631     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5632                                MethodHandle target,
5633                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5634         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5635         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5636         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5637         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5638             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5639         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5640             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5641         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5642         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5643         if (test == null) {
5644             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5645         }
5646         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5647     }
5648 
5649     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5650         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5651     }
5652 
5653     /**
5654      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5655      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5656      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5657      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5658      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5659      * <p>
5660      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5661      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5662      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5663      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5664      * <p>
5665      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5666      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5667      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5668      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5669      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5670      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5671      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5672      * T target(A..., B...);
5673      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5674      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5675      *   try {
5676      *     return target(a..., b...);
5677      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5678      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5679      *   }
5680      * }
5681      * }</pre></blockquote>
5682      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5683      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5684      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5685      * <p>
5686      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5687      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5688      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5689      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5690      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5691      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5692      * @param target method handle to call
5693      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5694      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5695      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5696      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5697      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5698      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5699      *          not match in their return types and their
5700      *          corresponding parameters
5701      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5702      */
5703     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5704                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5705                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5706         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5707         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5708         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5709             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5710         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5711             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5712             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5713         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5714             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5715         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5716         if (handler == null) {
5717             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5718         }
5719         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5720     }
5721 
5722     /**
5723      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5724      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5725      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5726      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5727      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5728      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5729      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5730      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5731      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5732      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5733      */
5734     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5735         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5736             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5737         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5738     }
5739 
5740     /**
5741      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5742      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5743      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5744      * <p>
5745      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5746      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5747      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5748      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5749      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5750      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5751      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5752      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5753      * </ul>
5754      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5755      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5756      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5757      * <p>
5758      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5759      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5760      * <p>
5761      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5762      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5763      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5764      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5765      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5766      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5767      * <p>
5768      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5769      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5770      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5771      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5772      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5773      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5774      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5775      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5776      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5777      * <p>
5778      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5779      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5780      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5781      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5782      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5783      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5784      * <a id="astar"></a>
5785      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5786      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5787      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5788      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5789      * <p>
5790      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5791      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5792      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
5793      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
5794      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
5795      * <p>
5796      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
5797      * <a id="effid"></a>
5798      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
5799      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
5800      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
5801      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
5802      * that longest list.
5803      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
5804      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
5805      * <p>
5806      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
5807      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
5808      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
5809      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
5810      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
5811      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
5812      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
5813      * </ol>
5814      * <p>
5815      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
5816      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
5817      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
5818      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
5819      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
5820      * iteration variable type.
5821      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
5822      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
5823      * </ol>
5824      * <p>
5825      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
5826      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
5827      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
5828      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
5829      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
5830      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
5831      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
5832      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
5833      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
5834      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
5835      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
5836      * the "internal parameter list".
5837      * </ul>
5838      * <p>
5839      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
5840      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
5841      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
5842      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
5843      * type.
5844      * </ol>
5845      * <p>
5846      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
5847      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
5848      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
5849      * </ol>
5850      * <p>
5851      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
5852      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5853      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
5854      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
5855      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
5856      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
5857      * </ol>
5858      * <p>
5859      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
5860      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
5861      * type.
5862      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
5863      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
5864      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
5865      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
5866      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
5867      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
5868      * loop return type.
5869      * </ol>
5870      * <p>
5871      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
5872      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
5873      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
5874      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
5875      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
5876      * pad out the end of the list.
5877      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
5878      * </ol>
5879      * <p>
5880      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
5881      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
5882      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5883      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5884      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
5885      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
5886      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
5887      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
5888      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
5889      * </ol>
5890      * <p>
5891      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
5892      * <ul>
5893      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
5894      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
5895      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
5896      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
5897      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
5898      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
5899      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
5900      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
5901      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
5902      * </ul>
5903      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
5904      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
5905      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
5906      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
5907      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
5908      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
5909      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
5910      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
5911      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
5912      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
5913      * <p>
5914      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
5915      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
5916      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
5917      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
5918      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
5919      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
5920      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
5921      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
5922      * (in argument order).
5923      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
5924      * returns {@code false}.
5925      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
5926      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
5927      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
5928      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
5929      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
5930      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
5931      * except by throwing an exception.
5932      * </ol>
5933      * <p>
5934      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
5935      * <ul>
5936      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
5937      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
5938      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
5939      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
5940      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
5941      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
5942      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
5943      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
5944      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
5945      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
5946      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
5947      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
5948      * </ul>
5949      * <p>
5950      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
5951      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
5952      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
5953      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5954      * V... init...(A...);
5955      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
5956      * V... step...(V..., A...);
5957      * R fini...(V..., A...);
5958      * R loop(A... a) {
5959      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
5960      *   for (;;) {
5961      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
5962      *       v = s(v..., a...);
5963      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
5964      *         return f(v..., a...);
5965      *       }
5966      *     }
5967      *   }
5968      * }
5969      * }</pre></blockquote>
5970      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
5971      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
5972      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
5973      *
5974      * @apiNote Example:
5975      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5976      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5977      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
5978      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
5979      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
5980      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
5981      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
5982      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5983      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5984      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5985      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5986      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5987      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
5988      * }</pre></blockquote>
5989      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
5990      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5991      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5992      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
5993      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
5994      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
5995      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
5996      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5997      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5998      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
5999      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6000      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6001      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6002      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6003      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6004      * }</pre></blockquote>
6005      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6006      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6007      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6008      * static class FacLoop {
6009      *   final int k;
6010      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6011      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6012      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6013      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6014      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6015      * }
6016      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6017      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6018      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6019      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6020      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6021      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6022      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6023      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6024      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6025      * }</pre></blockquote>
6026      *
6027      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6028      *
6029      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6030      *
6031      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6032      *
6033      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6034      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6035      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6036      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6037      * @since 9
6038      */
6039     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6040         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6041         loopChecks0(clauses);
6042 
6043         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6044         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6045         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6046         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6047 
6048         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6049             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6050             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6051             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6052             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6053         });
6054 
6055         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6056         final int nclauses = init.size();
6057 
6058         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6059         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6060         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6061             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6062             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6063             if (in == null && st == null) {
6064                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6065             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6066                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6067                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6068             } else {
6069                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6070             }
6071         }
6072         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6073                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6074 
6075         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6076         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6077         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6078 
6079         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6080         // Step 1D: check other types.
6081         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6082         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6083                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6084         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6085         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6086 
6087         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6088         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6089         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6090         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6091 
6092         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6093         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6094             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6095             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6096                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6097             }
6098             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6099                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6100             }
6101             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6102                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6103             }
6104             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6105                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6106             }
6107         }
6108 
6109         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6110         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6111         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6112         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6113         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6114         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6115 
6116         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6117                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6118         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6119                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6120 
6121         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6122     }
6123 
6124     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6125         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6126             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6127         }
6128         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6129             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6130         }
6131         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6132             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6133         }
6134     }
6135 
6136     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6137         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6138             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6139                     st.type().returnType());
6140         }
6141     }
6142 
6143     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6144         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6145         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6146                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6147                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6148                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6149                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6150                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6151         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6152     }
6153 
6154     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6155         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6156         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6157     }
6158 
6159     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6160         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6161         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6162         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6163     }
6164 
6165     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6166         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6167                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6168             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6169                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6170         }
6171     }
6172 
6173     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6174         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6175                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6176             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6177                     loopReturnType + ")");
6178         }
6179 
6180         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6181             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6182         }
6183         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6184                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6185             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6186         }
6187     }
6188 
6189     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6190         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6191                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6192             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6193                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6194         }
6195     }
6196 
6197     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6198         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6199             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6200             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6201             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6202         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6203     }
6204 
6205     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6206         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6207     }
6208 
6209     /**
6210      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6211      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6212      * <p>
6213      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6214      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6215      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6216      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6217      * <p>
6218      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6219      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6220      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6221      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6222      * <p>
6223      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6224      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6225      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6226      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6227      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6228      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6229      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6230      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6231      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6232      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6233      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6234      * additional state variable of the loop.
6235      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6236      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6237      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6238      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6239      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6240      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6241      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6242      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6243      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6244      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6245      * </ul>
6246      * <p>
6247      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6248      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6249      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6250      * from the external parameter list.
6251      * </ul>
6252      * <p>
6253      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6254      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6255      * passed to the loop.
6256      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6257      * V init(A...);
6258      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6259      * V body(V, A...);
6260      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6261      *   V v = init(a...);
6262      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6263      *     v = body(v, a...);
6264      *   }
6265      *   return v;
6266      * }
6267      * }</pre></blockquote>
6268      *
6269      * @apiNote Example:
6270      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6271      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6272      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6273      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6274      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6275      *   zip.add(a.next());
6276      *   zip.add(b.next());
6277      *   return zip;
6278      * }
