6279      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6280      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6281      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6282      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6283      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6284      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6285      * }</pre></blockquote>
6286      *
6287      *
6288      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6289      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6290      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6291      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6292      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6293      *     MethodHandle[]
6294      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6295      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6296      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6297      * }
6298      * }</pre></blockquote>
6299      *
6300      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6301      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6302      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6303      *             above for other constraints.
6304      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6305      *             See above for other constraints.
6306      *
6307      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6308      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6309      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6310      *
6311      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6312      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6313      * @since 9
6314      */
6315     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6316         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6317         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6318         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6319         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6320         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6321     }
6322 
6323     /**
6324      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6325      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6326      * <p>
6327      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6328      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6329      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6330      * <p>
6331      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6332      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6333      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6334      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6335      * <p>
6336      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6337      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6338      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6339      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6340      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6341      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6342      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6343      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6344      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6345      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6346      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6347      * additional state variable of the loop.
6348      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6349      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6350      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6351      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6352      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6353      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6354      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6355      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6356      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6357      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6358      * </ul>
6359      * <p>
6360      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6361      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6362      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6363      * from the external parameter list.
6364      * </ul>
6365      * <p>
6366      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6367      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6368      * passed to the loop.
6369      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6370      * V init(A...);
6371      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6372      * V body(V, A...);
6373      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6374      *   V v = init(a...);
6375      *   do {
6376      *     v = body(v, a...);
6377      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6378      *   return v;
6379      * }
6380      * }</pre></blockquote>
6381      *
6382      * @apiNote Example:
6383      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6384      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6385      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6386      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6387      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6388      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6389      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6390      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6391      * }</pre></blockquote>
6392      *
6393      *
6394      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6395      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6396      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6397      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6398      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6399      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6400      *     return loop(clause);
6401      * }
6402      * }</pre></blockquote>
6403      *
6404      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6405      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6406      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6407      *             See above for other constraints.
6408      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6409      *             above for other constraints.
6410      *
6411      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6412      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6413      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6414      *
6415      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6416      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6417      * @since 9
6418      */
6419     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6420         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6421         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6422         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6423         return loop(clause);
6424     }
6425 
6426     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6427         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6428         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6429         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6430         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6431         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6432         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6433         if (returnType == void.class) {
6434             // OK
6435         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6436             // leading V argument missing => error
6437             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6438             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6439         } else {
6440             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6441         }
6442         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6443         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6444                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6445             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6446         }
6447         if (init != null) {
6448             MethodType initType = init.type();
6449             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6450                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6451                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6452             }
6453         }
6454     }
6455 
6456     /**
6457      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6458      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6459      * <p>
6460      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6461      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6462      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6463      * <p>
6464      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6465      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6466      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6467      * <p>
6468      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6469      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6470      * iteration variable.
6471      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6472      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6473      * <p>
6474      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6475      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6476      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6477      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6478      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6479      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6480      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6481      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6482      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6483      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6484      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6485      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6486      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6487      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6488      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6489      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6490      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6491      * additional state variable of the loop.
6492      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6493      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6494      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6495      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6496      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6497      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6498      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6499      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6500      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6501      * </ul>
6502      * <p>
6503      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6504      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6505      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6506      * from the external parameter list.
6507      * </ul>
6508      * <p>
6509      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6510      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6511      * arguments passed to the loop.
6512      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6513      * int iterations(A...);
6514      * V init(A...);
6515      * V body(V, int, A...);
6516      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6517      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6518      *   V v = init(a...);
6519      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6520      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6521      *   }
6522      *   return v;
6523      * }
6524      * }</pre></blockquote>
6525      *
6526      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6527      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6528      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6529      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6530      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6531      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6532      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6533      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6534      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6535      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6536      * }</pre></blockquote>
6537      *
6538      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6539      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6540      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6541      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6542      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6543      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6544      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6545      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6546      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6547      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6548      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6549      * }</pre></blockquote>
6550      *
6551      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6552      * as loop parameters:
6553      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6554      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6555      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6556      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6557      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6558      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6559      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6560      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6561      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6562      * }</pre></blockquote>
6563      *
6564      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6565      * to enforce a loop type:
6566      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6567      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6568      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6569      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6570      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6571      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6572      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6573      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6574      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6575      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6576      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6577      * }</pre></blockquote>
6578      *
6579      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6580      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6581      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6582      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6583      * }
6584      * }</pre></blockquote>
6585      *
6586      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6587      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6588      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6589      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6590      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6591      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6592      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6593      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6594      *             See above for other constraints.
6595      *
6596      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6597      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6598      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6599      *
6600      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6601      * @since 9
6602      */
6603     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6604         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6605     }
6606 
6607     /**
6608      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6609      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6610      * <p>
6611      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6612      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6613      * values of the loop counter.
6614      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6615      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6616      * <p>
6617      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6618      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6619      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6620      * <p>
6621      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6622      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6623      * iteration variable.
6624      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6625      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6626      * <p>
6627      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6628      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6629      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6630      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6631      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6632      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6633      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6634      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6635      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6636      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6637      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6638      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6639      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6640      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6641      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6642      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6643      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6644      * additional state variable of the loop.
6645      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6646      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6647      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6648      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6649      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6650      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6651      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6652      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6653      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6654      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6655      * to the external parameter list.
6656      * </ul>
6657      * <p>
6658      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6659      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6660      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6661      * from the external parameter list.
6662      * </ul>
6663      * <p>
6664      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6665      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6666      * arguments passed to the loop.
6667      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6668      * int start(A...);
6669      * int end(A...);
6670      * V init(A...);
6671      * V body(V, int, A...);
6672      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6673      *   int e = end(a...);
6674      *   int s = start(a...);
6675      *   V v = init(a...);
6676      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6677      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6678      *   }
6679      *   return v;
6680      * }
6681      * }</pre></blockquote>
6682      *
6683      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6684      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6685      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6686      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6687      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6688      *     // the following semantics:
6689      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6690      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6691      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6692      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6693      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6694      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6695      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6696      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6697      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6698      *     }
6699      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6700      *     MethodHandle[]
6701      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6702      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6703      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6704      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6705      * }
6706      * }</pre></blockquote>
6707      *
6708      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6709      *              See above for other constraints.
6710      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6711      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6712      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6713      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6714      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6715      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6716      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6717      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6718      *             See above for other constraints.
6719      *
6720      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6721      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6722      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6723      *
6724      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6725      * @since 9
6726      */
6727     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6728         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6729         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6730         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6731         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6732         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6733         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6734         MethodHandle retv = null;
6735         if (returnType != void.class) {
6736             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6737             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6738             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6739         }
6740         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6741         MethodHandle[]
6742             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6743             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6744             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6745         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6746     }
6747 
6748     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6749         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6750         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6751         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6752         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6753         if (counterType != int.class) {
6754             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6755             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6756         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6757             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6758             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6759         }
6760         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6761         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6762         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6763         // strip leading V value if present
6764         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6765         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6766             // argument list has no "V" => error
6767             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6768             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6769         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6770             // missing I type => error
6771             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6772             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6773         }
6774         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6775         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6776             // special case; take lists from end handle
6777             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6778             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6779         }
6780         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6781         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6782             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6783         }
6784         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6785             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6786             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6787         }
6788         if (init != null) {
6789             MethodType initType = init.type();
6790             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6791                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6792                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6793             }
6794         }
6795     }
6796 
6797     /**
6798      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
6799      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6800      * <p>
6801      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
6802      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
6803      * <p>
6804      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6805      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6806      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6807      * <p>
6808      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6809      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6810      * iteration variable.
6811      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6812      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6813      * <p>
6814      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6815      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6816      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
6817      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6818      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6819      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
6820      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6821      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6822      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6823      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
6824      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6825      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
6826      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
6827      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6828      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6829      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6830      * additional state variable of the loop.
6831      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6832      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6833      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6834      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6835      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6836      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6837      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6838      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
6839      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
6840      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
6841      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
6842      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6843      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6844      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
6845      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
6846      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
6847      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
6848      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6849      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
6850      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
6851      * </ul>
6852      * <p>
6853      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
6854      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
6855      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
6856      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6857      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
6858      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
6859      * <p>
6860      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6861      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6862      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6863      * from the external parameter list.
6864      * </ul>
6865      * <p>
6866      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6867      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
6868      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
6869      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6870      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
6871      * V init(A...);
6872      * V body(V,T,A...);
6873      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
6874      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
6875      *   V v = init(a...);
6876      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
6877      *     T t = it.next();
6878      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
6879      *   }
6880      *   return v;
6881      * }
6882      * }</pre></blockquote>
6883      *
6884      * @apiNote Example:
6885      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6886      * // get an iterator from a list
6887      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
6888      *   r.add(0, e);
6889      *   return r;
6890      * }
6891      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6892      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
6893      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
6894      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
6895      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
6896      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
6897      * }</pre></blockquote>
6898      *
6899      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
6900      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6901      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6902      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
6903      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6904      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6905      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
6906      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
6907      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
6908      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6909      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6910      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6911      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6912      *     }
6913      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
6914      *     MethodHandle[]
6915      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
6916      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
6917      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6918      * }
6919      * }</pre></blockquote>
6920      *
6921      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
6922      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
6923      *                 See above for other constraints.
6924      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6925      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6926      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6927      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6928      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
6929      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6930      *             See above for other constraints.
6931      *
6932      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
6933      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
6934      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
6935      *
6936      * @since 9
6937      */
6938     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6939         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
6940         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6941         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
6942         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
6943         MethodHandle startIter;
6944         MethodHandle nextVal;
6945         {
6946             MethodType iteratorType;
6947             if (iterator == null) {
6948                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
6949                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
6950                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
6951             } else {
6952                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
6953                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
6954                 startIter = iterator;
6955             }
6956             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6957             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
6958 
6959             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
6960             try {
6961                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
6962                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
6963             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
6964                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
6965             }
6966         }
6967 
6968         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
6969         if (returnType != void.class) {
6970             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6971             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6972             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6973             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6974         }
6975 
6976         MethodHandle[]
6977             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
6978             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
6979         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6980     }
6981 
6982     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6983         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6984         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6985         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6986         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
6987         // strip leading V value if present
6988         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6989         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6990             // argument list has no "V" => error
6991             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6992             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6993         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
6994             // missing T type => error
6995             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
6996             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6997         }
6998         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
6999         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7000         if (iterator != null) {
7001             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7002             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7003             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7004                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7005             }
7006             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7007             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7008                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7009             }
7010             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7011                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7012                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7013             }
7014         } else {
7015             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7016                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7017                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7018                 // of Iterable
7019                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7020                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7021             } else {
7022                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7023                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7024                 // assignable to Iterable
7025                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7026                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7027                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7028                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7029                 }
7030             }
7031         }
7032         if (init != null) {
7033             MethodType initType = init.type();
7034             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7035                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7036                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7037             }
7038         }
7039         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7040     }
7041 
7042     /*non-public*/
7043     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7044         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7045         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7046         int[] order = new int[arity];
7047         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7048         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7049         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7050         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7051         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7052         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7053     }
7054 
7055     /**
7056      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7057      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7058      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7059      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7060      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7061      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7062      * <p>
7063      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7064      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7065      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7066      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7067      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7068      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7069      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7070      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7071      * <p>
7072      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7073      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7074      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7075      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7076      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7077      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7078      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7079      * </ul>
7080      * <p>
7081      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7082      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7083      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7084      * the cleanup.
7085      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7086      * V target(A..., B...);
7087      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7088      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7089      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7090      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7091      *   try {
7092      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7093      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7094      *     throwable = t;
7095      *     throw t;
7096      *   } finally {
7097      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7098      *   }
7099      *   return result;
7100      * }
7101      * }</pre></blockquote>
7102      * <p>
7103      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7104      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7105      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7106      * <p>
7107      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7108      * always throws.
7109      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7110      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7111      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7112      * <p>
7113      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7114      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7115      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7116      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7117      * <p>
7118      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7119      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7120      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7121      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7122      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7123      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7124      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7125      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7126      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7127      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7128      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7129      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7130      *
7131      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7132      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7133      *
7134      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7135      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7136      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7137      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7138      *          not match in their return types and their
7139      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7140      *
7141      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7142      * @since 9
7143      */
7144     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7145         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7146         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7147 
7148         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7149 
7150         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7151         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7152         // target parameter list.
7153         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7154 
7155         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7156         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7157         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7158 
7159         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7160         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7161     }
7162 
7163     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7164         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7165         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7166             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7167         }
7168         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7169         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7170             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7171         }
7172         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7173             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7174         }
7175         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7176         // target parameter list.
7177         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7178         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7179             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7180                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7181         }
7182     }
7183 
7184 }
